<div id="review_64972385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64972385" />
    <a title="Debbie Robson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1743317-debbie-robson"><img alt="Debbie Robson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493107767p2/1743317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64972385?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie Robson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie Robson" href="/user/show/1743317-debbie-robson">Debbie Robson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64972385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1474268819842120502">What a delight! I've always felt that the 1950s is a neglected decade as far as fiction goes and in Eva Rice's hands the decade (or at least the years 1954/55) are tellingly drawn. I love the descriptions and the feel of the house Magna, the parties at Dorset House and the Ritz and the afternoons at Aunt Clare's. <br/>This is an intelligent and atmospheric book which is very well written. It is a pity because of these things that there were a few discrepancies. For one I couldn't get Penelope's age r</span>
  <span id="freeText1474268819842120502" style="display:none">What a delight! I've always felt that the 1950s is a neglected decade as far as fiction goes and in Eva Rice's hands the decade (or at least the years 1954/55) are tellingly drawn. I love the descriptions and the feel of the house Magna, the parties at Dorset House and the Ritz and the afternoons at Aunt Clare's. <br />This is an intelligent and atmospheric book which is very well written. It is a pity because of these things that there were a few discrepancies. For one I couldn't get Penelope's age right no matter how I worked it - the mother three months pregnant when she was married in 1937 does not add up to a daughter who is 18 in November 1954 and just a few other odd things that should have been picked up by even the most cursory of edits. There was a confusion between a meeting with Harry, once written up as Wednesday afternoon, and a paragraph below as Thursday afternoon and then a chapter which suggested the passing of time and the coming of spring when all that the reader was dealing with seemed to be the passing of two days. <br />Perhaps I've got myself confused over these issues so would love other reader's comments. <br />Despite these quibbles and I'm pointing the finger at the publisher not Eva Rice - this is a must read and in my opinion is not Chick Lit, although some editions of the book look like its being marketed as such.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1474268819842120502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uH3k/FbHfHMk+SZW7uwikarJV/GDwh2CDeyT4ef09OGL8Qv7kT2QRrqv4fi43VsW5I1rhnUJNbEvFlDZPa+AHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9k7q9hvTzMCuPRY1EAZqvE2V61SbZT/n+1FNYQ+Otw3FwgXx3Ckg9TBr0ZtGNxM7A9HXI22uF9TZq45Z1dXD8w==')})
  }

          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
